item_0.note: The Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-1210] case involving client Destiny Adkins was the subject of a comprehensive file reorganization performed by Roscoe, an AI paralegal. Using an eight-bucket system, Roscoe organized 284 files, representing 86% of the target. The categorized totals are Litigation 211, Investigation 23, Lien 11, Expenses 7, Medical Records 7, Client 3, and Insurance 2. All files were renamed to follow the convention: YYYY-MM-DD - Client - Category - Originator - Description. 

There are 39 files remaining in the root that require manual review. This set includes 17 hash-named .md files that have not been processed, 20 .eml files representing litigation correspondence, and 6 .doc files in an unreadable binary format that will need conversion to PDF.

In the quality review, the error rate was 5.6% (7 out of 125 files). Corrections included fixing date errors, recategorizing one police report, and removing one wrong case file (dated [DOB-1209]) that pertained to a different incident than the [DOB-1208] case.

Case insights reveal a complex multi-party matter with co-plaintiff Juanita Downs. Defendants include Stephanie Nail (vehicle owner), Demetrius Turner (driver who fled the scene), and Allstate Insurance. A bad faith claim against Allstate has been bifurcated and placed in abeyance. Turner has an extensive criminal history and was difficult to locate for deposition. The vehicle was reported stolen after the accident (not before), which led to an initial denial of coverage by Allstate. There are active discovery disputes with Turner’s counsel, Rice Gumm PLLC, concerning deposition scheduling and overdue discovery responses, which exceed 60 days overdue as of November 1, 2024.

There are four files that require attorney review due to unclear or future dates, requiring verification from CourtNet or the client.

All reports have been saved to the Reports/ folder. Next steps include the manual categorization of the remaining 39 files, converting the six .doc files to PDF, and verifying dates for the flagged documents with CourtNet or the client.

Tuttle’s signature identifies her role, provides her contact information (D: [PHONE-37]; O: [PHONE-1173] ext 104; E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com) and notes “PLEASE NOTE NEW EMAIL ADDRESS.” The Whaley Law Firm is located at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222.

A subsequent message from Stempien on March 4, 2025 asked whether a date had been set for the deposition, providing his firm’s office and contact information.

The scheduling discussions stretch back to February 2025 and involved multiple participants from both sides, including Krista Rice of Rice Gumm PLLC and Eric Rice, with input from Stempien. On February 6, 2025, Krista Rice asked whether any of the proposed dates would work or if additional information was needed. In response, Sarena Tuttle indicated that the issue was not the dates but the start time, explaining that the deposition should occur during normal business hours and that an hour and a half was not sufficient to conduct a proper deposition. She asked for a valid reason if Demetrius Turner could not appear at 1:00 p.m. or earlier, warning that failure to do so could render him uncooperative and might prompt another motion to compel.

In an email dated February 6, 2025, Eric S. Rice (Rice Gumm, PLLC) advised that Bryce could file a motion and argued that there was no evidence Turner was driving and that Turner had already provided a sworn statement indicating he was not driving, along with the listed insured and vehicle owner. He suggested explaining why a 3:30 p.m. start had been chosen for the 20th. This message, like others from Eric Rice, contains the customary confidentiality and privilege notices, including a disclaimer that no attorney–client relationship is created by sending or receiving emails, along with the standard IRS Circular 230 warnings about tax disclosures contained in such communications.

Throughout the exchange, the parties circulated a mix of proposed dates and times, with one reference to a start time of 3:30 p.m. being discussed for the 20th, and with ongoing questions about Turner’s availability and the length of the deposition. The March 5, 2025 email ultimately announces a formal deposition notice for Demetrius Turner set for April 17, 2025 at 12:00 p.m. at Rice Gumm PLLC, with the Notice attached and the option to contact The Whaley Law Firm directly with any questions.

item_8.note: Case: Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-44]. Client: Destiny Adkins. This matter concerns Adkins & Downs v. Nail, et al.

In this matter, a deposition was being scheduled for a person referred to as Turner. As of March 4, 2025, the deposition had not yet been scheduled. In an email from Sarena M. Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, she informed Brian Stempien that Bryce was in a deposition out of town that day and that she would follow up with him upon his return later that afternoon. The message also noted Sarena’s contact details and her new email address.

Earlier email traffic, beginning in February 2025, revolved around scheduling that same deposition. On February 6, Krista Rice of Rice Gumm, PLLC wrote that Mr. Turner was not available until 3:30 p.m. and asked whether any of the dates 3/6, 3/12, 3/13, 3/19, or 3/20 would work. In response, Sarena Tuttle asked for a valid reason for Turner’s unavailability before 3:30 p.m., explaining that start time is the issue and that an hour and a half is not sufficient to conduct a proper deposition; she warned that without a valid reason Turner could be considered uncooperative and that a motion to compel might be forthcoming. Krista Rice followed up, asking to confirm whether any of the proposed dates would work or if additional dates were needed.

The thread also included additional correspondence from Eric S. Rice of Rice Gumm, PLLC. In a February 6, 2025 email, Eric advised Bryce that a motion could be filed and argued to the judge that there is no evidence Turner was driving, noting that Turner had already provided a sworn statement that he was not driving, along with the listed insured and the vehicle owner. He also suggested explaining why 3:30 p.m. on the 20th would be acceptable, framing it as not a difficult issue.

Throughout the exchanges, standard confidentiality and privilege notices appeared in the email signatures. For example, there were disclaimers stating that the information was attorney-privileged and confidential, that no attorney‑client relationship was created by sending or receiving the email, and that tax-related disclaimers under IRS Circular 230 applied to any tax-advice content. The signatures also reiterated that viewing, copying, disclosure, or distribution could be restricted, and they provided contact information for the parties involved.

In sum, by early February 2025 the parties were negotiating deposition dates for Turner, with Turner said to be unavailable before 3:30 p.m. on dates including March 6, 12, 13, 19, and 20. The discussion included whether to proceed with a motion to compel and how to justify a 3:30 start time, with particular emphasis on the possibility that the 3:30 time on the 20th could work. By March 4, 2025, however, the deposition had not yet been scheduled, and Sarena indicated that Bryce was again unavailable due to a deposition out of town, promising to follow up upon his return later that afternoon.

item_9.note: Destiny Adkins is the client in the matter labeled Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-46], and the case at issue is Adkins & Downs v. Nail, et al. A scheduling conversation among counsel in February 2025 concerned taking the deposition of a defendant named Turner in this case. The email chain includes participants from two Louisville law firms: Rice Gumm, PLLC, and The Whaley Law Firm, along with Brian Stempien of Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC. The correspondence reveals a dispute over when Turner could be deposed and how long the deposition should last, with repeated references to the need for a normal business-hours start time.

On February 6, 2025, Krista Rice of Rice Gumm, PLLC asked whether proposed deposition dates would work, listing options of February 24, 26, 27, or 28. She noted a scheduling conflict for February 20 and asked for guidance on which dates might be workable. Earlier that same morning, Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm replied to Krista, stating that the 24th—a Monday—was reserved for local motion hour and the 28th—a Friday—was Fayette motion hour, and that they were available only on the 26th or 27th, with a required start time of 1:00 p.m. She emphasized that an earlier start would be necessary and warned that Turner’s unavailability at that time could be interpreted as uncooperative, potentially leading to another motion to compel.

Krista responded later that day, confirming the scheduling need and asking whether any of the proposed dates would work or if additional options were needed. A separate note from Krista then stated that Mr. Turner would not be available until 3:30 p.m. and asked whether dates such as March 6, 12, 13, 19, or 20 would work. In response, Sarena questioned whether there was a valid reason for Turner’s unavailability before 3:30 p.m., reiterating the concern about the start time and the need for Turner to appear during normal business hours.

Krista followed up again, asking for confirmation that any of the proposed dates would work or whether more options were needed. Sarena pressed for the reason behind Turner’s late-hour availability, reiterating that the issue was not the dates themselves but the start time, and warning that Turner could be deemed uncooperative without a valid reason for a 1:00 p.m. or earlier start. Eric Rice then weighed in, suggesting that Bryce could file a motion and that they could inform the judge that there was no evidence Turner was driving and that Turner had already provided a sworn response stating he was not driving, alongside the listed insured and vehicle owner. Eric added that it would also be appropriate to explain why 3:30 p.m. could work for the 20th, noting that this should not be a difficult matter.

Separately, on March 4, 2025, Brian D. Stempien of Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC sent an email asking, “Did you guys get a date for this depo?” He provided the table of the case details and listed contact information for himself and colleagues, including his office in Louisville, KY, and the firm’s website. The message bore the standard attorney-privilege and confidentiality notices common to law firms, including disclaimers that sending an email does not establish an attorney-client relationship and that the content is intended for the named recipient. The email also referenced IRS Circular 230 disclosures for any tax-related content.

In short, the February 2025 emails show opposing counsel negotiating deposition dates for Turner, with Whaley Law Firm seeking to start at 1:00 p.m. due to court-motion hours on certain days, while Rice Gumm, PLLC proposed later start times (3:30 p.m. or later) and suggested alternative dates in March. The discussions repeatedly centered on whether Turner could be deposed during normal business hours and whether a shorter deposition duration (an hour and a half) would be sufficient. The participants debated the need for a valid reason if Turner could not start by 1:00 p.m., and there was a suggestion that a motion to compel could be filed if cooperation could not be achieved. By early March, counsel were still working toward obtaining a suitable deposition date, with Brian Stempien following up on whether a date had been set.

item_10.note: In February 2025, the Destiny-Adkins-MVA case Destiny Adkins and Juanita Downs v. Nail, et al. moved into deposition scheduling for the defendant, Mr Turner. The Whaley Law Firm, representing Destiny Adkins, coordinated with Rice Gumm, PLLC, which represented the other side, to arrange Mr Turner’s deposition in the Adkins & Downs matter (Adkins MVA dated [DOB-1163]; Downs MVA dated [DOB-1162]).

On February 5, 2025, at about 12:00 PM, Sarena Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager at The Whaley Law Firm, emailed Eric Rice (and others) asking whether February 20, 2025 at 3:30 PM at Rice & Gumm would work for Mr Stempien. The email thread included Destiny Adkins’ and Juanita Downs’ file references in the Filevine project addresses. Eric Rice replied later that Mr Turner would appear at Rice & Gumm’s office. In response, Sarena asked if there was a valid reason for Mr Turner’s unavailability before 3:30 PM, warning that without a valid reason for an appearance at 1:00 PM or sooner, he could be deemed uncooperative and that Whaley Law Firm would be forced to file another motion to compel.

Earlier that same day, Krista Rice of Rice Gumm, PLLC had indicated a scheduling conflict for February 20 and proposed alternative dates: February 24, February 26, February 27, or February 28. In the subsequent exchanges, the parties discussed start times and availability. Krista’s message noted that Mr Turner would be unavailable on those proposed dates before 3:30 PM, and that they should consider later times or different dates.

The Whaley firm responded on February 6 with scheduling constraints of their own. Sarena explained that February 24 was the Monday local motion hour and February 28 was Fayette motion hour, so they were available on February 26 or 27 only, but they required an earlier start time of 1:00 PM. Krista replied that Mr Turner was not available until 3:30 PM and asked whether the March dates would work: March 6, March 12, March 13, March 19, or March 20, 2025. Sarena followed up, asking for a valid reason for Turner’s unavailability prior to 3:30 PM if that time could not be accommodated, reiterating the concern about the start time.

Throughout the exchange, multiple emails carried confidentially notices and standard notices about privileged information. The threads show the following participants and contacts: Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; D: [PHONE-50]; O: [PHONE-51] ext. 104; E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com; note of a new email address), Krista Rice and Eric Rice of Rice Gumm, PLLC (address: 12804 Townepark Way, Ste. 200, Louisville, KY 40243; phone: [PHONE-52]; email: [EMAIL-53]; website: www.ricegummlaw.com), and other listed participants in the CC line (Bryce Koon, Daniel Gumm, Brian Stempien, and Mr. Stempien’s associated firms). The thread also includes references to the Destiny Adkins MVA and Juanita Nicole Downs MVA project addresses in Filevine.

In sum, the parties were actively negotiating deposition timing for Mr Turner, with the Whaley side insisting on a 1:00 PM start time or earlier and warning of a motion to compel if a valid justification for later starts could not be provided. The defense, however, indicated availability only after 3:30 PM, proposing dates in March (the 6th, 12th, 13th, 19th, or 20th) and prompting continued discussion about acceptable times and legitimate reasons for the scheduling constraint.

item_19.note: Case: Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-98]. The client in this matter is Destiny Adkins, and the case caption is Adkins & Downs v. Nail, et al., with the underlying matter dated [DOB-99].

Initial scheduling attempt (January 21, 2025). W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, wrote to request Mr. Turner’s deposition availability for the coming weeks in the Adkins & Downs v. Nail case. He asked the opposite counsel to provide times that would work for scheduling the deposition.

Follow-up on January 28, 2025. Bryce Koon followed up again, requesting an update on Mr. Turner’s deposition availability.

Response from January 31, 2025. Eric S. Rice, Partner at Rice Gumm, PLLC, replied that he had not yet been able to speak with his client. His message included his contact information: [PHONE-100] and [EMAIL-101], along with the Rice Gumm firm address, and carried the standard confidentiality notice.

Proposed times (February 4, 2025). Eric Rice advised that Mr. Turner could be available at 3:30 p.m. on February 12, 14, 18, 19, or 20, 2025, if those dates worked. The message was sent from Rice Gumm, PLLC, with Eric Rice’s signature block and the firm’s contact details.

Proposed date narrowed (February 5, 2025, 12:00 PM). Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, responded that the only date that works for their office from the previously listed options is February 20, 2025. She noted that they had several mediations and depositions scheduled for February and asked whether Mr. Turner would still be incarcerated or if the deposition would take place at Rice Gumm’s office; if the client remained incarcerated, they would need to check with the jail regarding process and availability. Her message included her contact details and new email address.

Confirmation of the February 20 date (February 5, 2025, 1:50 PM). Eric Rice replied that Mr. Turner would be “here at my office,” confirming his client’s availability for the deposition at Rice Gumm, PLLC. The signature block again provided Rice Gumm’s contact information.

Follow-up on the 3:30 p.m. time (February 5, 2025, 1:56 PM). Sarena Tuttle thanked Eric Rice for the confirmation and asked Mr. Stempien whether February 20, 2025 at 3:30 p.m. at Rice & Gumm would work for him, including her standard sign-off with her contact details.

Schedule conflict introduced (February 6, 2025, 14:35:04 +0000). Krista Rice, Firm Administrator at Rice Gumm, PLLC, emailed to note a scheduling conflict for February 20 and to request alternative dates. She proposed February 24, 26, 27, or 28 as possible options and asked the recipients to advise which of those dates would work. Her message included her full contact information and the firm’s address.

Additional context and participants. The email chain involves multiple parties: Krista Rice (Rice Gumm, PLLC) as the sender of the February 6 note; Sarena M. Tuttle (The Whaley Law Firm) as Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager; Eric S. Rice (Rice Gumm, PLLC) as Partner; W. Bryce Koon (The Whaley Law Firm); Destiny Adkins (MVA client from [DOB-1109]); and Juanita Nicole Downs (MVA 4/16/2021) referenced in the Filevine project addresses. The communications were exchanged among these parties with copies to additional firm personnel, and all emails contained standard confidentiality notices. The case involves the deposition of Mr. Turner related to the Adkins & Downs v. Nail, et al. matter, with the deposition location and timing being negotiated across January and February 2025. The conference chain shows a preference for February 20 at Rice Gumm, but scheduling conflicts necessitated alternative dates (2/24, 2/26, 2/27, or 2/28) as of the latest note.

item_20.note: Case: Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-104]. The client is Destiny Adkins and the matter captioned Adkins & Downs v. Nail, et al. is a motor vehicle accident case arising from an event on [DOB-105]. This note records a sequence of email communications among counsel regarding scheduling Mr. Turner’s deposition.

In the email thread, dated February 21, 2025 (transmitted through multiple messages in late January and early February 2025), The Whaley Law Firm’s Bryce W. Koon and Sarena Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager for the firm, coordinated with Eric S. Rice of Rice Gumm, PLLC, and Daniel Gumm. The cc list also included Brian Stempien, Destiny Adkins’ Filevine project address, and Juanita Nicole Downs’ Filevine project address, along with Destiny Adkins’ and Juanita Downs’ Filevine project emails. The subject line referenced the case Adkins & Downs v. Nail, et al.

On January 21, 2025, Bryce Koon requested counsel’s assistance in scheduling Mr. Turner’s deposition and asked for his availability in the coming weeks. He requested a prompt reply and signaled that the deposition would be part of ongoing litigation management. He closed with his endorsement and firm contact information from The Whaley Law Firm.

Bryce followed up on January 28, 2025, writing, “Good afternoon counsel, I am writing to follow up on my previous request. Any update is appreciated,” again requesting Mr. Turner’s deposition availability. His message included his standard firm contact details and a note indicating this electronic communication is intended only for the named recipient and may contain privileged information.

On January 31, 2025, Eric S. Rice replied that he had not yet been able to speak with his client. He signed as a partner of Rice Gumm, PLLC, with the firm’s Louisville, Kentucky office address and contact information, and with the usual confidentiality notice following his message.

The thread progressed on February 4, 2025, when Eric Rice sent a response stating that Mr. Turner could be available at 3:30 p.m. on February 12, February 14, February 18, February 19, or February 20, if those dates were workable. He again included his contact details and the firm’s confidentiality notice.

Sarena Tuttle replied on February 5, 2025, indicating that February 20 is the only date that would work for The Whaley Law Firm due to their calendar of mediations and depositions for the month. She asked for clarification on whether Mr. Turner would still be incarcerated or if the deposition would take place at Rice Gumm’s office. She noted that if Mr. Turner remained incarcerated, the parties would need to check with the jail regarding process and availability. This message included her updated contact details, including a new email address, and the firm’s standard disclosure about confidentiality and privileged information.

In summary, the deposition scheduling efforts involve coordinated efforts between The Whaley Law Firm and Rice Gumm, PLLC, with proposed dates centered on February 12, 14, 18, 19, and 20 at 3:30 p.m., and a constraint from The Whaley Law Firm that only February 20 would work given their existing mediation and deposition load, plus a live question about Mr. Turner’s incarceration status and whether the deposition would be held at the defense counsel’s office or at the opposite party’s location. The Filevine project emails for Destiny Adkins and Juanita Downs were included in the correspondence as part of the case file tracking.

item_21.note: On February 5, 2025, Sarena Tuttle, a litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager at The Whaley Law Firm, sent an email to Mr. Eric S. Rice of Rice Gumm, PLLC, regarding the Adkins & Downs v. Nail, et al. matter ( Destiny Adkins, the client in Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-1104]). The message noted that February 20th is the only date out of a list that works for The Whaley Law Firm, as they already have several mediations and depositions scheduled for the month. Sarena asked whether Mr. Turner would still be incarcerated or if the deposition could take place at Rice Gumm’s office, and she added that if Mr. Turner remains incarcerated they would need to check with the jail about its process and availability. The email was sent from Sarena to Eric and was CC’d to Bryce Koon, Daniel Gumm, Brian Stempien, Destiny Adkins MVA [DOB-1103] - Filevine Project Email Address, and Juanita Nicole Downs MVA 4/16/2021 - Filevine Project Email Address. Sarena included her work contact information and noted a new email address.

This exchange followed prior scheduling inquiries regarding Mr. Turner’s deposition. On February 4, 2025, Eric S. Rice replied to Bryce Koon, stating that Mr. Turner could be available at 3:30 p.m. on February 12, 14, 18, 19, or 20, if those dates worked. Eric’s message included his professional contact details and a confidentiality notice, consistent with the firm’s standard email format.

Earlier in the chain, on January 31, 2025, Eric Rice had written to Bryce Koon and Daniel Gumm, with Brian Stempien and the Destiny Adkins MVA and Juanita Nicole Downs MVA filevine project emails CC’d, to indicate that he had not yet been able to speak with his client. He signed as a partner of Rice Gumm, PLLC, with his contact information and the confidentiality notice.

Prior to that, on January 28, 2025, Bryce Koon had sent a message to Eric Rice and Daniel Gumm, with Brian Stempien and the same Filevine project emails CC’d, requesting an update and following up on his previous request regarding Mr. Turner’s deposition. The message concluded with Bryce’s firm details and a standard confidentiality notice.

Going further back, on January 21, 2025, Bryce Koon had written to counsel requesting assistance in scheduling Mr. Turner’s deposition and asking for availability for the coming weeks. This message also included Bryce’s contact information and a confidentiality notice.

The email chain thus documents ongoing efforts to schedule Mr. Turner’s deposition in the Adkins & Downs v. Nail, et al. case, with multiple parties copied and a preference established for conducting the deposition on February 20, 2025, pending Mr. Turner’s incarceration status and the logistics of where the deposition would occur.

item_22.note: Case: Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-1101]. Client: Destiny Adkins. The matter at issue is Adkins & Downs v. Nail, et al. This note summarizes a February 2025 email thread between The Whaley Law Firm and Rice Gumm, PLLC regarding scheduling a deposition for Mr. Turner in the Adkins/Downs matter.

Participants and contact details
- The Whaley Law Firm: Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager, based at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222. Direct dial [PHONE-1100]; Office [PHONE-1099] ext 104. Email: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com (note: new email address). The firm’s address and the telephone numbers appear in the signature blocks.
- Rice Gumm, PLLC: Eric S. Rice, Partner, located at 12804 Townepark Way, Suite 200, Louisville, KY 40243. Office phone [PHONE-113]; Email: [EMAIL-114]. Website: www.ricegummlaw.com.
- Other counsel copied in the thread include Bryce Koon, Esq. (The Whaley Law Firm), Daniel Gumm (Rice Gumm, PLLC), Brian Stempien (address shown as That Attorneys.com in the CC), and filevine-backed project email addresses for Destiny Adkins MVA and Juanita Nicole Downs MVA.
- Filevine project emails: Destiny Adkins MVA [DOB-1096] - [EMAIL-116]; Juanita Nicole Downs MVA 4/16/2021 - [EMAIL-117].

Timeline and key details
- February 5, 2025, 12:00 PM: Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm wrote to Eric Rice (and CC’d others) in response to a scheduling request. She stated that the only date that works for their office is February 20, 2025. She noted they have several Mediations and Depositions scheduled that month and asked whether Mr. Turner would be incarcerated or would attend the deposition at Rice Gumm’s office; if incarcerated, they would need to check with the jail about processes and availability. The message included Sarena’s standard signature and confidentiality notice.
- February 5, 2025, around 1:50 PM: Eric S. Rice replied to Bryce and Daniel Gumm (and cc’d others). He indicated that Mr. Turner could be available at 3:30 PM on February 12, 14, 18, 19, or 20 if those dates worked.
- February 5, 2025, 1:56 PM: Sarena Tuttle responded, thanking Mr. Rice for the information and asking whether Mr. Stempien could confirm whether February 20, 2025 at 3:30 PM at Rice & Gumm would work for him.
- February 5, 2025, 3:30 PM (approximate in thread time): Eric Rice replied with a concise note: “He’ll be here at my office.” This affirmed that Mr. Turner would attend the deposition at Rice Gumm’s office.
- February 5, 2025, 3:56 PM (approximate): Sarena followed up with a final confirmation email. She thanked Mr. Rice for the confirmation and again asked Mr. Stempien to confirm whether February 20, 2025 at 3:30 PM at Rice & Gumm would work for him. Her signature block was included with the Whaley Law Firm contact information.

Location and logistical considerations
- The deposition location discussed is Rice Gumm, PLLC, at their Louisville office. There is explicit discussion of whether Mr. Turner would appear in person at Rice Gumm’s office or if his incarceration status would affect the process; if incarcerated, jail procedures and availability would need to be checked. The suggested deposition date that ultimately appeared viable for the Whaley office was February 20, 2025, at 3:30 PM.

Confidentiality and boilerplate
- Each email in the thread carried the standard confidentiality notice typical of attorney communications, reminding recipients that the message may contain privileged information and should not be disclosed or forwarded by unintended recipients.

In summary, the parties coordinated by email to schedule Mr. Turner’s deposition in the Adkins & Downs v. Nail case, with February 20, 2025 at 3:30 PM at Rice Gumm, PLLC identified as the workable slot for the Whaley Law Firm, contingent on confirmation from Mr. Stempien. Eric Rice indicated Mr. Turner would be present at Rice Gumm’s office, and the thread includes the involved counsel and relevant filevine addresses for Destiny Adkins and Juanita Downs.

item_31.note: The case Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-1048] involves Destiny Adkins and Juanita Nicole Downs against Demetrius E. Turner and potentially others, arising from a motor vehicle accident that occurred on April 16, 2021. The matter is currently in the discovery phase, with depositions being scheduled. The review of activity for this case covers the period from December 25, 2024 to January 24, 2025.

The most recent activity shows Bryce Koon, the plaintiffs’ attorney, requesting to schedule Mr. Turner’s deposition. However, there is a discrepancy in the record: Mr. Turner has claimed that he was not driving at the time of the incident, which conflicts with the plaintiffs’ understanding of events. This discrepancy is a potential red flag that may require further investigation and could impact the case strategy.

The recommended next steps are to review any evidence that could establish Mr. Turner was driving on the day of the accident, as suggested by opposing counsel Eric Rice, and to follow up on obtaining Mr. Turner’s responses to discovery requests if they have not already been received.

item_55.note: Destiny Adkins is the client in a motor vehicle collision matter captioned Adkins & Downs v. Turner, et al. in Jefferson Circuit Court (docket 22-CI-002878). The case file for Destiny Adkins, associated with the MVA occurring on [DOB-921], contains a sequence of email communications between The Whaley Law Firm and Rice Gumm, PLLC regarding a motion and discovery responses. The correspondence involves Destiny Adkins and Juanita Nicole Downs as co-parties in the matter, with cc recipients including Destiny Adkins MVA and Juanita Nicole Downs MVA Filevine project email addresses, as well as Brian Stempien of That Attorneys, and Daniel Gumm of Rice Gumm.

On November 12, 2024, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, sent a message to Eric S. Rice and Daniel Gumm, with cc to the Destiny Adkins MVA Filevine project email address, the Juanita Nicole Downs MVA Filevine project email address, and Brian Stempien. The subject was Adkins & Downs v. Turner, et al. (Jefferson Circuit 22-CI-002878). In that email, Bryce attached the motion filed that day and informed counsel that the motion was set for Monday, November 25, 2024. He stated that if he received the clients’ responses prior to that date, he would remand the motion and invited any questions.

Later, on November 21, 2024, at 10:22 a.m., Eric Rice replied. He explained that he had spoken with Demetrius that morning and that he would be leaving the following day to go home for Thanksgiving, returning December 2. He would not be able to meet with Demetrius until December 4 to obtain discovery responses. Rice asked Bryce to remand his motion-to-compel (MTC).

Shortly thereafter, at 10:47 a.m. on the same day, Bryce Koon responded. He thanked counsel for the update and acknowledged that the responses had been outstanding for some time. He stated that he owed it to his clients to ensure progress, and he agreed to roll the motion two weeks to December 9, 2024. Bryce explained that this extension would allow counsel to meet with their client, and he added that should he receive the responses by that date, he would remand his motion.

The message from Bryce also included his firm’s contact information: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone [PHONE-291]; fax [PHONE-292]. Eric Rice’s message included his contact information for Rice Gumm, PLLC: [PHONE-293]; [EMAIL-294]; 12804 Townepark Way, Ste. 200, Louisville, KY 40243; website www.ricegummlaw.com. The email chain also contained standard confidentiality and attorney‑client privilege notices referencing that the electronic messages and attachments may contain legally privileged information, and instructions to contact the sender if received in error and not to disclose or forward the information.

In sum, the parties discussed a motion in the Adkins & Downs v. Turner case, with a schedule contingent on obtaining discovery responses. Bryce initially set the motion for November 25, 2024, with a potential remand if responses were received. Eric Rice indicated he could not secure discovery responses until December 4, due to Thanksgiving travel, and requested remand of the MTC. Bryce agreed to extend the deadline to December 9, 2024, contingent on receiving the necessary discovery responses by that date, and confirmed his intent to remand if those responses were supplied.

item_70.note: Destiny Adkins is the client in the motor-vehicle-accident matter styled Destiny Adkins, et al. v. Stephanie Nail, et al., Jefferson Circuit Court, case number 22-CI-002878. The matter is identified in the record as the Destiny-Adkins-MVA case with the underlying event on April 16, 2021. The listed client for this matter is Destiny Adkins.

On January 16, 2024, a communication concerning the Destiny Adkins v. Nail case was sent from W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, to Brian D. Stempien and an address at [EMAIL-376], with Sarena Tuttle cc’d. The subject line read Destiny Adkins, et al. v. Stephanie Nail, et al. (Jefferson Circuit 22-CI-002878). In the body, Bryce Koon stated, “Good afternoon counsel, Please see attached filed today in Jefferson Circuit Court. Thank you, W. Bryce Koon, Esq.” The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information appeared beneath, including its Louisville, Kentucky address at 712 Lyndon Lane, and phone and fax numbers. The message carried the standard attorney-privileged and confidential notice, cautioning that the email is intended only for the named recipient and that disclosure, distribution, or use by others is prohibited; it also included the usual disclaimer that no attorney-client relationship is created by sending or receiving the email, and directed the recipient to consult the firm’s website for the disclaimer. The email also contained the IRS Circular 230 tax disclosure warning, noting that tax advice in the document may be limited and that the recipient may not rely on any tax advice in it to avoid penalties.

On July 22, 2024, at 5:13 PM, Brian D. Stempien, of Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC, sent a reply to Bryce Koon and Aaron Whaley, with Sarena Tuttle cc’d, regarding the same Jefferson Circuit Court case (Destiny Adkins, et al. v. Nail, 22-CI-002878). The subject line echoed the prior matter. In the body, Stempien wrote, “Aaron and Bryce: Are you guys going to let Ms. Nail out of this case? Give me a call if you would like to discuss.” Stempien’s firm information followed, including its address at the Jefferson Marders Building, 11507 Main Street, Middletown Historic District, Louisville, KY 40243, plus office numbers [PHONE-834], fax [PHONE-833], toll-free [PHONE-379], and the email [EMAIL-380], with the firm’s website listed as http://www.thslaw.co. The message again included the Privileged and Confidential notice restricting dissemination, the statement that no attorney-client relationship is created by email, and the IRS Circular 230 tax-disclosure warning.

Earlier, on January 16, 2024, Bryce Koon’s January email was followed by the standard Privileged and Confidential notice and the same disclaimers regarding attorney-client privilege and the lack of an established attorney-client relationship, as well as the Circular 230 tax warning. The January message reiterated that the attached filing had been submitted in Jefferson Circuit Court for Destiny Adkins, et al. v. Stephanie Nail, et al., case number 22-CI-002878, and listed Bryce Koon’s firm details and contact information from The Whaley Law Firm.

In sum, the record reflects three key communications around the Destiny Adkins matter in Jefferson Circuit Court: (1) a January 16, 2024 email from Bryce Koon noting an attachment filed that day; (2) a July 22, 2024 reply from Brian Stempien asking if Ms. Nail would be released from the case and inviting discussion; and (3) a September 3, 2024 email from Brian Stempien reiterating the inquiry with the line, “Are you going to let my lady out of this case?” Each message includes the standard Privileged and Confidential notice, no attorney-client relationship clarification, and the Circular 230 tax warnings, and each identifies the same case caption and docket (Destiny Adkins v. Stephanie Nail, Jefferson Circuit 22-CI-002878). The parties to the correspondence include Destiny Adkins, the Whaley Law Firm (Bryce Koon and Aaron Whaley), and Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC (Brian D. Stempien), with Sarena Tuttle cc’d on the communications.

item_71.note: Case: Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-829]. Client: Destiny Adkins. This note covers the Destiny Adkins v. Stephanie Nail et al. matter in Jefferson Circuit Court, case number 22-CI-002878, with the underlying motor-vehicle accident having occurred on April 16, 2021. The file, titled “RE: Destiny Adkins, et al. v. Stephanie Nail, et al. (Jefferson Circuit 22-CI-002878),” includes a sequence of email exchanges dated in July and September 2024 between counsel at Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC and The Whaley Law Firm, regarding the possible dismissal of Destiny Adkins from the case and related conditions.

On July 22, 2024, at 5:13 PM, Brian D. Stempien of Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC sent an email to Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm (with Aaron Whaley also copied, along with Sarena Tuttle and two Filevine project email addresses for Destiny Adkins MVA [DOB-828] and Juanita Nicole Downs MVA 4/16/2021). The subject line mirrored the case caption. In the body, Stempien asked, “Are you guys going to let Ms. Nail out of this case? Give me a call if you would like to discuss.” His signature block followed, including his firm’s address at the Jefferson Marders Building, 11507 Main Street, Middletown Historic District, Louisville, KY 40243, phone numbers, fax, toll-free line, and website. The message carried the customary attorney-privilege and confidential-information notices, including a disclaimer that no attorney-client relationship is established by email, and standard IRS Circular 230 tax-disclosure language.

Earlier that same day (or in the same thread), the parties’ contact blocks again show the involved offices and the same confidentiality and privilege disclaimers.

On September 3, 2024, later in the day, Brian Stempien sent a message to Bryce Koon (and others on the original thread). The subject line again referenced Destiny Adkins, et al. v. Stephanie Nail, et al. While the note itself is short, it reads, “Are you going to let my lady out of this case?” followed by Stempien’s contact and disclaimer block. The message reiterated the ongoing concern about Destiny Adkins’ status in the case and included the same privilege/confidentiality language, the “No Attorney-Client Relationship” disclaimer, and the Circular 230 tax-warning text.

Also on September 3, 2024, Bryce Koon replied to Brian Stempien. The email, dated around 12:19 PM, stated: “Good afternoon Brian, We will agree to dismiss your client from the case if she amends her Answer and/or discovery responses to state that Defendant Turner was operating her vehicle with permission. Outside of that, I do not believe we can agree to voluntary dismissal of your client. If you have any questions in this regard, please feel free to contact me at the number below.” The reply was sent with Bryce Koon’s signature block for The Whaley Law Firm at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, including a phone number and fax number. The message was accompanied by the firm’s standard confidentiality notice, including a note that an image in the signature had been removed by the sender, and the usual “This electronic message is intended only for the named recipient” disclaimer.

Finally, at approximately 4:33 PM (UTC) on September 3, 2024, Brian Stempien responded to the thread with the line: “Yeh.. not going to happen. I guess we will have to file something.” He again included his standard signature block and the same Privileged and Confidential language and the no-attorney-client-relationship disclaimer commonly included in outgoing emails for his firm.

Throughout the thread, the participants, in addition to Stempien (Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC) and Koon (The Whaley Law Firm), included Aaron Whaley and Sarena Tuttle on the Whaley side, plus Destiny Adkins MVA [DOB-827] - Filevine Project Email Address and Juanita Nicole Downs MVA 4/16/2021 - Filevine Project Email Address as CC recipients in the earliest message. The correspondence also references, and is accompanied by, the standard “Privileged and Confidential” notices and the disclaimer about no attorney-client relationship, as well as the IRS Circular 230 tax-disclosure language.

The communication trail reflects an ongoing strategic discussion about whether Destiny Adkins would be dismissed from the case, and under what conditions that dismissal could occur. Specifically, Bryce Koon proposed that Destiny could be dismissed if she amended her Answer and/or discovery responses to state that Defendant Turner was operating her vehicle with permission; otherwise, a voluntary dismissal of Destiny Adkins was not anticipated. The sequence shows that Brian Stempien pushed for a prompt resolution that would remove Destiny from the case, while stating his intent to “file something” if a resolution could not be reached. The record also preserves the contact details for the two law firms and the Filevine project email addresses tied to Destiny Adkins and Juanita Nicole Downs, as well as the standard legal disclaimer language that accompanied every transmission.

Stephanie Nail, et al., Jefferson Circuit Court case 22-CI-002878 (designated in the file as Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-386]), is the subject of an email exchange dated September 3, 2024. The correspondence involves counsel Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm and Brian D. Stempien of Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC, along with several other recipients listed in the CC field, including Destiny Adkins MVA-related Filevine project emails and Juanita Nicole Downs MVA-related Filevine project emails. The overall topic concerns possible dismissal of certain parties from the case and the conditions for such dismissal, within the context of the Jefferson Circuit Court docket.

On January 16, 2024, Bryce Koon sent an email to Brian Stempien and [EMAIL-387], with Sarena Tuttle CC’d, under the subject Destiny Adkins, et al. v. Stephanie Nail, et al. (Jefferson Circuit 22-CI-002878). In that message, Koon wrote: “Good afternoon counsel, Please see attached filed today in Jefferson Circuit Court.” The email was sent from The Whaley Law Firm, with Bryce Koon’s contact information provided: W. Bryce Koon, Esq., The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; Phone: [PHONE-823]; Fax: [PHONE-389]. The message carried the standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer and related notices typical of such communications, including statements about no attorney-client relationship arising from the transmission and references to IRS Circular 230 disclosures where applicable.

On July 22, 2024, Brian D. Stempien replied to Bryce Koon and Aaron Whaley, with Sarena Tuttle CC’d, under the subject Destiny Adkins, et al. v. Stephanie Nail, et al. (Jefferson Circuit 22-CI-002878). In his message, Stempien asked: “Aaron and Bryce: Are you guys going to let Ms. Nail out of this case? Give me a call if you would like to discuss.” He signed with his firm’s contact details: Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC, Jefferson Marders Building, 11507 Main Street, Middletown Historic District, Louisville, KY 40243; Office: [PHONE-390]; Fax: [PHONE-391]; Toll Free: 1-[PHONE-392]; Email: [EMAIL-393]; Website: http://www.thslaw.co. The message included the firm’s customary privileged and confidential notices, confirming that no attorney-client relationship is created by receipt and reiterating the standard disclaimers and policy statements common in such communications. The email chain also includes references to the attachments and a general warning about privilege and tax-disclosure requirements as part of the signature blocks, mirroring the practice seen in other emails from the same exchanges.

Earlier in the chain, on September 3, 2024, at approximately 12:10 PM, Stempien sent a follow-up message asking: “Guys: Are you going to let my lady out of this case?” This message, like the others, included Stempien’s contact information and the firm’s customary confidentiality and privilege notices, including explicit disclaimers about attorney-client relationships and the guidelines required by IRS Circular 230. The signature block contains his office address in Louisville, with the same general warnings about confidentiality and the prohibition on disseminating the content if the recipient is not the intended recipient.

Shortly thereafter, at 12:19 PM on the same day, Bryce Koon replied to Brian Stempien with a direct conditional offer: “Good afternoon Brian, We will agree to dismiss your client from the case if she amends her Answer and/or discovery responses to state that Defendant Turner was operating her vehicle with permission. Outside of that, I do not believe we can agree to voluntary dismissal of your client.” He provided his standard Whaley Law Firm signature, including the firm’s Louisville address (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222), phone number [PHONE-394], and fax [PHONE-395]. The message again carried the firm’s privilege and confidentiality notices and related disclaimers.

In sum, the September 2024 email thread shows ongoing settlement discussions about voluntary dismissal of a party from Destiny Adkins v. Stephanie Nail, et al., with a specific condition: the opposing party would be dismissed if Destiny Adkins’ Answer and/or discovery responses were amended to assert that Defendant Turner operated the vehicle with permission. Absent that amendment, the parties indicated they were not willing to pursue voluntary dismissal. The correspondence also reflects a broader pattern of coordination among counsel across the Whaley Law Firm and the Stempien firm, the inclusion of multiple Filevine project email addresses in CC lines, and the presence of standard attorney-client privilege and confidentiality notices in each message.

item_74.note: The case is Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-796], with client Destiny Adkins, and in Jefferson Circuit Court the matter ADKINS, DESTINY ET AL v. NAIL, STEPHANIE M. item_129.note: Case: Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-668]. The client is Destiny Adkins.

This note concerns the matter of Adkins and Downs v. Nail, et al., in Jefferson Circuit Court, case number 22-CI-002878. The record is drawn from a chain of emails between counsel regarding the case.

On September 28, 2023, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, wrote to counsel about the Adkins matter. He stated, “Please see attached filed today in Jefferson Circuit Court.” His message included his standard firm signature with the firm’s contact information: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone [PHONE-669]; fax [PHONE-670]. He also included the usual attorney-client privilege disclaimer, noting that the electronic message is intended only for the named recipient and may contain privileged or protected information; if received in error, the recipient should contact The Whaley Law Firm, not use or forward the information, and no waiver of privilege would apply.

Earlier, on October 7, 2023, Brian D. Stempien of Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC, replied to Bryce Koon with a scheduling inquiry. He wrote: “Counsel: We were actually able to locate Ms. Nail. How does Wednesday, October 18 at 2 o’clock in our office work for you?” The message was sent from his iPhone and was copied to [EMAIL-671], Sarena Tuttle, and Beth Alexander. The subject line of this thread remained related to Adkins and Downs v. Nail, et al. (Jeff. Cir. 22-CI-002878).

On October 9, 2023, Bryce Koon responded to counsel with, “Counsel, This will work for us. Thank you.” His reply included the same standard confidentiality disclaimer as in his September 28 message. The communication confirms that the parties agreed to a meeting time and that the proposed date and the location—Ms. Nail’s appearance—were being scheduled in connection with the Jefferson Circuit Court case referenced above.

In sum, the email exchanges between The Whaley Law Firm and Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC, between September 28 and October 9, 2023, relate to a filing in Jefferson Circuit Court (case 22-CI-002878) and to scheduling a meeting concerning Ms. Nail for Wednesday, October 18, at 2:00 p.m. in the office of the opposing counsel. The thread also displays the standard privilege notices and contact information for the involved firms.

item_130.note: Case: Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-673]. Client: Destiny Adkins. This notes the matter Adkins and Downs v. Nail, et al. in Jefferson Circuit Court (case number 22-CI-002878). The following is a sequence of email communications among counsel for the parties.

On September 28, 2023, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, wrote to counsel with a brief update: please see the attached filing that was submitted today in Jefferson Circuit Court. The message included his firm’s contact information—The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone [PHONE-674]; fax [PHONE-675]—and carried a standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer stating the electronic message is intended only for the named recipient and that recipients should not use or forward the information if received in error. A spam- and virus-scan notice from Proofpoint Essentials appeared at the bottom of the email.

Two weeks later, on October 7, 2023, Brian D. Stempien, of Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC, replied to Bryce Koon with a scheduling proposal. He wrote that they had actually located Ms. Nail and asked whether Wednesday, October 18, at 2:00 p.m. in their office would work for Bryce Koon’s side. Stempien provided his firm’s details: Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC, in the Jefferson Marders Building, 11507 Main Street, Middletown Historic District, Louisville, KY 40243; office phone [PHONE-676]; fax [PHONE-677]; toll-free 1-[PHONE-678]; email [EMAIL-679].

On October 9, 2023, at 11:16 a.m., Bryce Koon replied, signaling agreement with the proposed arrangement. He wrote, “Counsel, This will work for us,” and included his standard firm signature and confidentiality disclaimer indicating the message is intended only for the named recipient and should not be used or shared if received in error. His contact details were The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone [PHONE-680]; fax [PHONE-681].

Later that same day, October 9, 2023, at 3:26 p.m. UTC, Brian Stempien sent a follow-up: “Assuming this works for Campbell, we will get this set up. Let me know if you are not alright with doing this here. I would like to minimize the logistical challenges for obvious reasons.” He closed with his Travis Herbert & Stempien signature block and the same standard privileged/ confidential notices. The email reiterated that the message and any attachments are intended for the recipient and that sending or receipt does not establish an attorney-client relationship; it also included the IRS Circular 230 tax information disclaimer about the disclosure obligations for tax advice in written communications.

The thread includes additional formalities typical of attorney communications. Bryce Koon’s messages consistently carried the confidentiality notices stating the electronic communication is for the named recipient and should not be disseminated if received in error, and Brian Stempien’s messages carried the same notices, including the standard disclaimer about no attorney-client relationship being established by sending or receiving emails and the IRS tax-advice warning where applicable.

Throughout, the exchanges were CC’d to additional recipients to share context: [EMAIL-682], Sarena Tuttle, and Beth Alexander, with the communications preserving their respective roles in the matter. The messages also contained the usual electronic-disclaimer language and a note that the emails may include attorney-privileged or otherwise protected information.

In summary, the communication chain from September 28 to October 9, 2023, reflects counsel coordinating a meeting to discuss the Adkins and Downs v. Nail matter, with a proposed in-office meeting to discuss Ms. Nail’s location (having located her) and a proposed date of Wednesday, October 18, at 2:00 p.m., contingent on Campbell’s agreement. The thread includes complete contact details for both law firms, standard confidentiality and privilege notices, and the customary notices about no attorney-client relationship being created by email.

He proposed trying to set the depositions of the opposing clients in June if possible and asked Sarena to contact Beth (Beth Alexander) regarding dates and other details; he also asked Aaron to call him when he had a moment. item_186.note: This note documents the deposition scheduling discussions in the Destiny Adkins personal injury matter (Adkins & Downs v. Stephanie Nail & Allstate). The exchange spans an April 2023 email and several June 2023 messages among the plaintiff’s and defense counsel, centered on arranging depositions for Ms. Nail and the other parties, with an emphasis on minimizing the number of depositions in one day.

On April 24, 2023, Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm informed Brian Stempien of Travis Herbert & Stempien that they were apologetic for the delay and attached the plaintiffs’ responses to discovery. She noted that deposition dates were flexible and asked whether counsel and their client were available on May 23, 25, 30, or June 1, and that depositions could be conducted either via Zoom or in the defense office. The email referenced attachments containing the plaintiffs’ responses to the discovery requests. Sarena’s signature blocks included her contact information and new email address.

On June 2, 2023, Brian Stempien responded to Aaron Whaley and Sarena, urging that the depositions for the clients be set in June if possible. He asked Aaron and Sarena to contact Beth concerning dates and indicated that Aaron should call him when available.

On June 6, 2023, at 10:51 AM, Sarena sent a reply to Beth Alexander stating that their office was available for depositions on June 20, 22, 27, or 29, and that they would like to take Mrs. Nail’s deposition on the same day, anticipating a full day for all three depositions. Sarena’s message was cc’d to Brian Stempien and Aaron Whaley, with her contact details reaffirmed in the signature block.

Later that same day, at 12:09 PM, Beth Alexander replied that June 29 was the only date among the proposed options on which Brian was available for two depositions; she noted that Brian would not agree to three depositions in one day and asked for alternative dates in the following week for scheduling Ms. Nail’s deposition at their office.

Also on June 6, at 12:23 PM, Sarena responded, acknowledging that three depositions in a single day are a lot. She suggested that because the week of the 4th of July is the following week, they could do the 6th, or, looking at the week after that, the 11th or 12th. Her message included her standard contact details and reiterated the scheduling possibilities.

For reference, the email chain included multiple professional signatures with the parties’ law firms and contact information, including Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm in Louisville, KY; Beth Alexander, paralegal to Brian Stempien at Travis Herbert & Stempien, Louisville; and Brian D. Stempien of Travis Herbert & Stempien, with their respective office addresses and telephone numbers. The thread also contained the customary attorney-privilege disclaimers typical of such communications.

In the matter of Adkins & Downs v Stephanie Nail & Allstate, the depositions scheduling discussions involved Destiny Adkins and several counsel and staff from two law firms. The earliest relevant communications in this thread begin with an email from Beth Alexander, paralegal to Brian Stempien of Travis Herbert & Stempien, to Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm (with copies to Brian Stempien and Aaron Whaley) on June 6, 2023. Beth notes that June 29 is the only date on which Brian is available to take two depositions in one day, and that Brian will not agree to three depositions in a single day. She asks Sarena to propose dates, perhaps the following week, to schedule Ms. Nail’s deposition at their office. Beth provides her contact information: Beth A. Alexander, Paralegal to Brian Stempien, Travis Herbert & Stempien, Jefferson Marders Building, 11507 Main Street, Louisville, KY 40243; phone [PHONE-928]; fax [PHONE-929]. The email thread includes standard attorney‑client privilege and confidentiality notices.

Earlier in the chain, Sarena Tuttle responds to Beth on the same day, June 6, 2023, at 10:51 AM. She states that their office is available for depositions on June 20, 22, 27, or 29, and that they would like to take Mrs. Nail’s deposition on the same day, anticipating a full day to cover all three depositions. Sarena signs as Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager for The Whaley Law Firm, with the firm’s Louisville address at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222. Her direct line is [PHONE-930], main line [PHONE-931] ext 104, and her email is Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, noting that it is a new address. This message also contains the standard privilege disclaimer and confidentiality notices.

The thread also contains prior scheduling discussions. On June 2, 2023, Brian Stempien wrote to Aaron Whaley and Sarena, urging that the depositions be scheduled in June if possible, and asking them to contact Beth concerning dates. He also asked Aaron to call him when possible. Brian’s contact details are listed as Travis Herbert & Stempien, Jefferson Marders Building, 11507 Main Street, Middletown Historic District, Louisville, KY 40243; Office [PHONE-932]; Fax [PHONE-933]; Toll Free 1-[PHONE-934]; email [EMAIL-935]; website http://www.thslaw.co. The message is accompanied by standard Privileged and Confidential notices.

Prior to June, the thread goes further back to an April 24, 2023, email from Sarena to Brian (with Aaron copied), in which she apologizes for a delay and attaches the Plaintiff’s Responses to Discovery Requests. She notes that deposition dates are fairly flexible and asks if the client is available on May 23, 25, 30, or June 1, offering to conduct the depositions via Zoom or at the client’s office. Earlier still, on April 21, 2023, Aaron Whaley forwarded a message from Brian Stempien to Aaron and to Beth Alexander. Brian explains that his insurer is pressuring him to file a motion to compel and asks for depositions and discovery dates, requesting that Aaron coordinate and provide the dates. Brian’s contact information (same as above) is included in this forwarded thread.

In summary, the deposition scheduling in this matter progressed through several correspondences from April through June 2023. Key points include:
- April 21, 2023: Brian requests deposition dates and discovery coordination; asks Aaron to assist and to coordinate with Beth.
- April 24, 2023: Sarena provides plaintiff discovery responses, proposes deposition dates (May 23, 25, 30, or June 1), and offers Zoom or in-office depositions; attachments are included.
- June 2, 2023: Brian asks to set depositions in June and to contact Beth for dates; requests a call.
- June 6, 2023: Sarena identifies available dates for depositions (June 20, 22, 27, or 29) and proposes taking Nail’s deposition the same day; anticipates a full day for all three depositions; notes Sarena’s new email address.
- June 6, 2023: Beth responds that June 29 is the only date Brian can accommodate for two depositions and that he will not agree to three in one day; she asks for alternative dates the following week to schedule Nail’s deposition at their office; provides Beth’s contact details.

All of these messages include the standard attorney-privilege and confidentiality disclosures, the practice of noting “No Attorney-Client Relationship,” and, in several emails, references to attached documents and image attachments referenced as embedded images within the messages. The communications collectively map out the coordination among Destiny Adkins’s case team and opposing counsel toward scheduling the depositions of Stephanie Nail and related parties.

item_236.note: Case: Destiny-Adkins-MVA-[DOB-1117]. The client is Destiny Adkins, and the matter is styled Adkins & Downs v. Stephanie Nail & Allstate. The communications spanning June and July 2022 involve counsel for Destiny’s side—the Whaley Law Firm—and counsel for Stephanie Nail’s side—Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC—with several recipients CC’d, including Sarena Tuttle, A. Campbell Ewen, and Beth Alexander. The exchange centers on service of process, extensions of time to respond, and potential amendment or settlement discussions in the underlying case following Destiny Adkins’s motor vehicle accident on April 16, 2021.

On June 30, 2022, Sarena M. Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm sent an email to Brian D. Stempien of Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC, with Aaron Whaley and A. Campbell Ewen also copied. In this message, Tuttle thanked Stempien for his letter dated June 28, 2022 noting representation of Stephanie Nail at the request of Allstate. She stated that the firm is open to settlement discussions at any time and, if an offer is forthcoming, is willing to discuss. However, she noted, per CourtNet, that Stephanie Nail had been served via Certified Mail on June 15, 2022, and Destiny’s team looked forward to receiving Nail’s Answer on or about July 15, 2022. Tuttle also advised that if further discussion or information was needed regarding settlement, contact could be made directly to discuss the claim in more detail, and she attached the Interrogatories propounded upon Nail along with the Complaint dated June 15, 2022. The message listed Sarena M. Tuttle’s contact information, including the Louisville, Kentucky address (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222) and phone numbers, and noted a new email address for correspondence. The email also included the customary firm signatures and disclaimers, including spam/virus scan notation from Proofpoint Essentials and the standard “Privileged and Confidential,” “No Attorney-Client Relationship,” andIRS Circular 230 disclosures typically accompanying such correspondence, as well as the firm’s disclaimer about the limitations of tax advice and the prohibition against using the document for marketing purposes. The message also contained the sender’s and recipients’ respective email signatures and contact details.

On July 14, 2022, at approximately 10:50 a.m., Brian D. Stempien replied to Aaron Whaley and Sarena Tuttle. He commented on service: the return attached to the electronic file on CourtNet allegedly shows the word “COVID” spelled out, and he stated that, in his view, this does not constitute effective service. He asked to be informed if there is a disagreement or if a motion for default is planned. He then recalled, or stated his recollection, that there had been a discussion about a 30-day extension of the time to Answer by agreement, and he asked to know whether the opposing party would be opposed to extending through August 1. He also asked whether the clients intended to move to amend the Complaint and suggested that if amendment is planned, it might be prudent to wait to see what happens when Nail is served with the amended complaint. The email concluded with Stempien’s standard contact information for Travis Herbert & Stempien, PLLC, including address in the Jefferson Marders Building, Louisville, KY, and telephone numbers, as well as the firm’s website.

At 11:02 a.m. on the same day, July 14, 2022, Aaron Whaley responded to Stempien. He stated that he had no objection to an extension through August 1, and that if Allstate were to extend coverage, he would have no objection to an indefinite extension while he attempted to resolve the claim with Allstate. His reply was also copied to Sarena Tuttle, A. Campbell Ewen, and Beth Alexander, and it was sent from Whaley’s email address [EMAIL-1118].

The record also reiterates that the parties referenced the CourtNet status with Nail’s service by Certified Mail on June 15, 2022, and there is ongoing discussion about extending deadlines, service validity, and the possibility of amending the Complaint. The messages include typical case-specific content such as the inquiry about a default motion should service be challenged, and whether an extension to August 1 would be opposed. The communications also reflect that counsel contemplated potential settlement discussions, the status of Nail’s service, and the procedural steps necessary to move the case forward, including whether to serve an amended complaint.

In addition to the substantive exchange, the emails carried standard firm-specific formalities: the July 14 emails included the usual privileged/confidentiality notices, no attorney-client relationship disclosures, and disclaimers regarding the IRS Circular 230 regulations governing tax advice in written communications. The correspondence also included boilerplate language about email disclaimers and the sender’s firm identity, with the final contact details for Aaron Whaley and The Whaley Law Firm in Louisville, Kentucky.

In sum, the matter Destiny Adkins v. Stephanie Nail & Allstate involved an ongoing dialogue in mid-2022 about service validity, deadlines to answer, potential amendments to the Complaint, and possible settlement discussions, all within the context of Destiny Adkins’s motor vehicle accident case arising on April 16, 2021. The parties agreed to consider extensions and contested service in the Courtnet record, while counsel also exchanged positions on settlement opportunities and the proper handling of the complaint and any amended pleadings.

Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm, with the same office address and contact numbers, and the same email, Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, again noting the new email address.
